Folks, VERY IMPORTANT! Please be aware that Mandy verbally said Baking Powder (NO) in the chicken marinade but meant Baking soda and did spell on the screen if you were using CC. She made up verbally in follow through PINCH OF BAKING SODA! i can't stress enough though to add salt throughout the cook a little at a time. I was so hesitant in mine because of all the soy sauce. So I sprinkled some salt on the whole pan after tasting it and it was an unbelievable difference. You will see. I though I had ruined the recipe but I saved it by sprinkling salt very carefully on the whole thing and then folks can salt their dish. Also it's not the same without a couple of fried eggs on top of your dish to let the yolk meld into the rice for creaminess and I never eat my fried rice without plain yogurt. Aloha, Hilo Paul

Wait so no sesame oil? Is sesame oil part of a different style or just completely wrong?
There is not one Oriental style restaurant within 50 miles that has a decent fried rice here.  The Thai place in Crystal River is a possibility, but, so far, I've only had noodles there.  Before Covid-19, they would not do take out, but, that may have changed.  I don't want to say something is not good if I've not tried it.  The norm is some peas and either minced or finely ground carrot.  You won't find chunks of anything.  Even roast pork is ground.  It's also flavorless.  Covid-19 is not why I make fried rice.  I make it because I love well-prepared and flavorful dishes.  This recipe looks similar to mine and she explains it very well.  Another thing you are hard pressed to find is egg in the mix.  Egg makes it substantial enough to have as a meal, meat or no meat.    Making a large batch, I will use 4 eggs and soft scramble them first. The only thing I would add is a bit of ginger over the carrots, grated or the powdered.  Not a lot, because it is strong.  Just a pinch in the amount of rice she made, and scant 1/2 tsp. in a large batch. I prefer large chunks of sweet onion, too. At the very end, right when you turn off the heat, add a  couple drops of sesame oil.  No more than that.  It's strong, but adds so much flavor.  In a large batch, 4-5 drops.  Taste before adding more.  All in all, this is a great cooking video.  You should mention day old rice in the beginning, because that, is key!
Also add a 1/4 tsp of Sesame Oil, fot an identical take out taste!

I have used this recipe several times as a general guideline for egg fried rice.  And just used 4 eggs.  Also, we can't have wheat so I use Tamari in place of soy sauce.  The other day I looked up what the difference is between light and dark soy sauce and the primary difference is dark soy sauce is fermented longer and has molasses.  So I made this again today and drizzled some molasses in.  OMG, took it to the next level of amazing and tasted even more like restaurant fried rice (which I haven't had in a couple of decades due to food intolerances).  For anybody who might need to omit soy altogether and might be using coconut aminos, I bet a drizzle of molasses would work to kick up the flavor as well.  Or if you can't find dark soy sauce.  Just use a tiny little bit of molasses though because its' very strong.  I used probably the equivalent of about a teaspoon.

Umm hello guys, I don't know if I should even be writing this, but I wanted to share my version of fried rice. Similar to hers, just a little tweaks  I marinate the chicken with salt, pepper, red chilli powder, minced garlic and lil bit of soya sauce. A second option for those who do not want the baking soda directly in their mix is to add it to their diced chicken or beef, let it sit for 10 minutes, and then wash it off well. This will create the same tenderizing effect on chicken or beef while getting rid of any excess baking soda. (Fun fact: If you listen closely, you can hear it sizzling during the process (: ) Enjoy!

I make a similar dish whenever I don't know what to make but have plenty of bits in the fridge. Sometimes I will use the flavored rice packages (Rice-a-roni) and while that or any rice is cooking, will have 2 deep pans like woks going - one to store and mix the cooked foods and one to cook each thing separately in. It is different every time because of what I choose to use or have on hand - sauteed canned mushrooms with butter and garlic, thin slices of weiners, or small strips of luncheon meat like Spam, can of cut green beans, cross cut small bits of celery, cabbage shreds, bits of green yellow or red peppers, bean sprouts, carrots, peas, finely cut leftover meats from fridge, onions or garlic, scrambled eggs just like this example, bits of bacon cut thinly, and any thing you can think of that you like separately. It will mix in with other things well. It is so easy to make a huge batch and store in containers in the fridge or freezer and then microwave to heat up. I spice it up with a little soya sauce and often use a separate dish of stir fry beef that I have marinated with garlic, soya sauce, sesame oil,  pepper, and tapioca starch so it makes a thick 'gravy like sauce' (add more water and stir up well if the tapioca starch has jelled the sauce too much), it will thin out nicely. The end result is good if you have a lot of color and an assortment of slightly fried browned meats to crunchy foods like the celery that has been sauteed. Thanks for reminding me of one of my favorite fast dish foods (20 minutes and it is all done). While you are frying up one or two similar ingredients, you are preparing or chopping the next to go in. This is the perfect late night snack or isolation dish.

Lovely recipe. Just a word of caution. The surface that you chopped the raw chicken is the same surface you placed the bowl afterwards. Presumably (during the edit) you cleaned the surface after chopping if not, the bottom of the bowl will transfer the raw chicken to other surfaces. I'm confident you did, but it's always worth mentioning it to viewers to protect them and to cover your self.

When we do fried rice at home I cut the carrots into thin strips, I use brown onion instead of red, I use frozen baby peas (thawed) and I use high quality oyster sauce (I use the Mega-Chef brand- they use more natural ingredients) and some home made stock with the veges. I use Braggs all purpose seasoning or liquid aminos which are basically soy sauce- but no GMOs or nasty chemicals added. I try to use more seasoning and less soy because soy isn't good for you consumed in large quantities.  I also find if I fry the rice in batches in my non stick electric wok, it doesn't stick at all so I use less oil (no matter how much I season my steel wok, or how much oil I put in- rice still  sticks in it). And I make myself an oil mixture by adding half and half pure beef dripping with coconut oil and a little sesame for flavor. I melt it and set it aside to use. I then use the sesame oil by itself near the end when I've mixed all the rice, egg and veges together. Our fried rice is better than anything we can buy at a takeout place or restaurant, and it does so many meals. It's even nice cold.

So much oil used, 1tbsp for eggs at the start, 2 tbsp for chicken/veggies, 2 tbsp for rice, that's 5 tbsp / 75 ml oil = 609 calories just for the oil part.    I usually only use 10ml of oil for 175g of rice with 100g eggs, 50g chicken, 50g veggies. 2ml for the eggs (2 or 3 pieces),  3ml for everything else chicken onions veggies, then the next 5ml for the rice. Non stick pan / teflon is better for cutting calories than a wok then. My whole fried rice is only about 600 calories.   I wonder about the stove used in here, is that a high pressure stove ?

The only thing that I would say is wrong about this recipe is cooking the eggs twice. You will have over cooked the egg and made them rubbery. Putting the egg in near the end will mean that they are cooked just the once and the egg soaks into the rice and chicken giving it an extra creamy taste to them.

Erm. Honestly, that is not Chinese Fried Rice.  Maybe it'd American Styled Chinese Fried Rice...no offense. Anyway..there is too much oil used, and soya sauce is a no-no for fried rice. This is pretty close to the method I use for fried rice. For the chicken marinade, I would add some sesame oil, and fresh garlic and ginger, and a shot of Chinese cooking wine if I have it available.  I would cook the eggs first, Chicken second, and remove them from the wok. Then I would fry the onions by themselves, and add the rice when they are about half-way cooked.  I use frozen peas and add them near the end of cooking, then add in the Chicken and eggs to heat them. Lastly a bit of soy sauce to season. Then it is ready to serve.
